<Text>Service Department.
My long-standing mechanic ran the diagnostic on my Mini and told me what was wrong and why an engine light was on. He recommended I go to the dealer for the repair.

I contacted another independent Mini garage for a second opinion. I learned that there was a factory warranty extension on the part that diagnosis #1 showed as failing. (high pressure fuel pump)

With reluctance this second source said go to Mini as it is a warranted repair. I told this garage that my first choice mechanic had reset the 'lights'. She told me that the computer in my car still retained the 'event' and that it would be found.

I went to Mini of Concord. I had to wait a week for am appointment that provided me with a loaner car. There are no repairs while you wait, even if it is only the $205 diagnosis. In on Thursday with the promise of an answer the following Tuesday. You read that right.

Mid afternoon the following Tuesday I received a call from the service rep that my car needed new plugs and the fuel injectors cleaned. $600. No mention of the high pressure fuel pump that was originally ferreted out by one source and confirmed to be problematic and warranty work by the second source.

I asked if the technician looked at the print-out I had brought indicating the problem was a fuel pump and was told the plugs and the injector cleaning were all that was needed.

The plugs were less than three months old. Factory equipment. Installed elsewhere when I had the car in for a scheduled service.

The service rep minimized the fuel injector clean out, likening it to a can of over the counter clean-out product and that the entire service wouldn't take that much longer. $600 and not the real problem.

Mini of Concord did not want to dedicate the time on their analysis equipment to 'reach deeper' into my car's computer. They are inundated with business since the closing of a nearby Mini dealership. They are ill-prepared with an overworked staff and wonderfully, overbooked for tons of future work.

The problem I wanted repaired remains unaddressed and according to  Mini of Concord they have no way of confirming the problem is real despite the independent print out I provided and ignoring the question as to their full, in-depth analysis capabilities.

I hope when this problem resurfaces and the engine goes to half-power as it is programmed to do, my family and I are not placed in peril. I no longer trust Mini of Concord</Text><date>1573399822409< /date></record>

<Name>Colleen Montoya</Name><time>1435350076798<//time><Rate>5</Rate>< Review>
My husband and I had been looking for a mini for me to replace my miata that got totaled for about 1 month. After a bad buy with a private party, we decided to go dealership route. My husband went to the SF dealership and they has what we wanted (older year Mini Cooper, hardtop S with low miles) but it wasn't on the lot yet. So we visited the Concord one. When we arrived on the lot someone immediately noticed us looking around and asked if we needed help, we did so they sent out a sales person. In comes Michael Chaves. We asked if they had anything like we were looking for. Turns out they had a lease return with less than 20,000 miles in great condition. But we weren't looking for something that new. (the one in SF was a 2002). We opted to check it out anyways. Michael was VERY knowledgeable about the cars. My husband (who drives and works on race cars) knew exactly what he wanted for me and Michael had answers. He even knew how much the car weighed when I asked, no hesitation. (I like light little cars, hence the miata before).  Michael did not pressure us, the car we were looking at was slated to be a CPO but hadn't been completed yet so it wasn't amazing looking. He explained what they do, what a CPO is, etc. We left without feeling like we were violated and tasked to think about it.

We discussed and my husband agreed I could get what I wanted, either the 2002 or the 2012. I hemmed and hawed up until the day we were scheduled to go in and buy. I felt if I didn't get the newer one, I would regret it. So I went with the 2012. Michael was ready for us, and so was the car (my baby car 2.0) when we arrived on Friday night. We test drove it (not necessary but fun) and then settled to agree on the terms. I had a concern that there was damage to the front bumper that hadn't been repaired. For my husband, this was a bargaining tool. In the end, we paid a price we were comfortable with AND they agreed to repair the bumper. Jason, who assisted with the sale was nice as well.

When they went to do the contract, there were others ahead of us and the wait was about an hour. We were able to leave and get dinner and come back when they were ready for us. I cannot remember the women who helped us with the contract but she was good also. After that was done, Michael gave me my keys (complete with Mini key chain!) and spent time showing me the features of the car. I really appreciated this since I am not use to a European car and some things were different, it helped a lot.

I read all the reviews on this dealer before going but I was set on this car and in the end, Michael was GREAT. The process was so smooth and he really made it easy without pressuring us. I would highly recommend this dealer and Michael if you are EVER looking for a Mini. I love my Mini Cooper!<//Review>

<Text>This was my first time buying a car, and Butch changed all my preconceptions of the 'slick' care salesman.

From the initial online inquiry into a pre-owned Mini, Butch was very transparent in what was available - providing detailed specs of all the pre-owned Minis. This was important to me as other salesmen who were closer to San Francisco played coy and gave vague details, all in hopes of getting someone into the dealership.

Once my girlfriend & I arrived at the dealership, Butch was very attentive as to what we were looking for - and didn't steer us to the more expensive option (as an aside, Mini Concord a great selection of pre-owned Countrymen in the B.A.).

In the end, we had a choice of two pre-owned cars with the options we were looking for. Throughout the process, Butch was helpful - he encouraged us to really test-drive both models and helped us get the best deal & financing.  And after the sale, he followed up with phone calls to see if we had any questions or issues with our purchase.

I would highly recommend Butch to anyone looking for a Mini - new or pre-owned.< /Text><Rating>5< /Rating>< Name>

<Review>Limon went upmarket to Fort Washington and has now dropped down even lower market than where they began near the Villagio shopping center, but the prices are stuck at Fort Washington levels, even though they are now located in a decidedly down market strip mall. The quality of the ingredients appears to have returned to their original levels, and that's a good thing.
The flavors of their food is amazing as always. They coarse cut the fish for their ceviche, which prevents the fish from devolving into a mush. The cheese empanadas are very plain and simple, but oh so delicious.The batter on their Jalea is light and crispy, not at all greasy. The seco de cordero is simply brilliant - well worth the visit.
I love the food there, but just last week, a light lunch for 2 there, without wine or beer was $80, so sadly I will not be going to Limon as often as I'd like to.< /Review>< pics>

< text>
The Peruvian food in this place is wonderful! There's choices for the meat eaters (chicken beef, seafood, fish, etc.), as well as the vegetarians (honestly, I didn't look for vegan items). I would highly recommend that first-timers try the lomo or pollo saltado and, for a little sweet alcoholic drink, the chichatini. They have a nice selection of wines as well. The peach bread pudding is also a great choice that rivals any bread pudding that Campagnia might offer. Ambiance wise, it's very nice, definitely nicer than its San Francisco parent. Highly recommend!< /text>

I've purchased 3 vehicles from this dealership over the years. My last car was in 2013.  I was not thrilled with the people and process then and wasn't likely to ever return. However, as a DGDG owned store, I figured I would at least talk to them after all they are very close to home.

I will advise all car buyers to do their research and do get prices over the internet before going to the dealer. My wife wanted an White 2020 Explorer ST and Capitol Ford had one, so last night I submitted a query on their website, including some information about what I wanted, my trade-in, the incentives, financing, and a specific vehicle, using the exact VIN.

I received a generated response from Ryan, then a follow-up call in the morning from Gerry. We agreed on price, they looked up my Ford Pass ID and subtracted an additional $750 from the price, gave me a price on my trade-in after I gave them the vehicle VIN, and they offered to bring the vehicle and paperwork to my Livermore residence, drop it off, go through the paperwork for correctness and signatures, go over the car functions, operations, and details, then take my trade in back to the dealership.

Gerry arrived at 2PM and did exactly that, then drove away..

<user>111120053729530637682</user><user_name>Hans Aichlmayr</user_name><Date>1575174176791</Date><rating>5< /rating>< Text>
I recently had a great experience purchasing a 2018 Ford Certified Used Expedition at Capitol Ford.  I found the vehicle on the web a mere three business days earlier and although the listing was too new for photos to be available, the dealership provided a wealth of information, e.g., Auto Check, and window sticker, that allowed me to scrutinize every feature and ultimately conclude that it was exactly what I wanted.    I also surmised that this vehicle would sell quickly because it has several features that are impossible to find in used offerings for this model.  Therefore I immediately contacted the dealership on-line and received a price quote from Donavan Jones---which was identical to the listing price.  A few correspondences later I made a test drive appointment.  In the interim, I used the wealth of data available on-line to estimate the full cost of the transaction,  then decided how I wanted to make the purchase, and finally obtained pre-approval for a loan from a local credit union that I concluded offered the best deal.

When I arrived for my appointment, I was greeted by a staff that was friendly, courteous, and professional despite it being a very busy post-holiday day.  Dino accompanied me on the test drive and thoroughly answered several technical questions that I had.  The drive went well and the vehicle met all of my expectations.  Upon return,  Dino let slip that many people were interested in the vehicle---and validated my hypothesis.  At the time I interpreted it to be an observation rather than a pressure tactic; I later learned that pressure tactics are discouraged at this dealership.  Whatever the case, it really didn't matter to me because I essentially made my decision to purchase before I stepped onto the lot and I arrived fully prepared to do so.

The actual purchase process took about 2.5 hours.  I didn't mind the wait at all because I recognized that there was a lot of paper to push and it basically went smoothly.  I was actually surprised that the whole process from test drive to having the keys in my hand could be accomplished in a few hours.  This was facilitated by the dealership's participation in the CUDL program---they even found a loan with a comparable term but better rate.

I was also presented with a lot of warranty and vehicle protection offerings.  These are tough calls because one must weigh the uncertain factors of long-term component reliability versus their potential cost to repair or replace.  For strictly mechanical components, long-term reliability is fairly well established and the odds of actually using a warranty are low.  Unfortunately, today's vehicles are becoming more like aircraft--notwithstanding Ford's aluminum bodies--in that they employ a myriad of electronic sensors and sub-systems that are less robust than mechanical components and ultimately more difficult to repair.  Consequently I opted for more warranty and protections than I would have twenty years ago.  In my opinion, the dealership could improve the experience by listing and explaining these options, their costs, and providing examples of how one could benefit from them and thus make informed choices.

All in all, I felt that the entire purchase experience was professional and fair. Given that the vehicle that I wanted was in high demand, there was no point to haggling.  Moreover, the asking price was clearly fair based on my survey of the market and third-party scoring.

Lastly, while I had really good luck in this whole endeavor, I greatly  appreciate that my evident preparation was recognized and that it contributed to getting me to the front of the line.

I wouldn't hesitate to make another purchase from this dealership in the future.  Although it could be very far in the future because I tend to keep my  vehicles for many years---I arrived in a truck that I have been driving for 26 years and the thought of parting with it is anathema.  Hopefully my new ride will have comparable longevity and bring me similar enjoyment.<//Text>

For my first car buying experience, it was bittersweet. My salesman David was very cordial and really worked to try to get me a vehicle that would fit my needs. Once I got in to sign the papers, my experience did not go so smoothly. I did not trust this, considering the contract we signed said any changes would have to be in writing. I called the next day and surprise, I DID have to sign something! Whether or not any of the interactions were intentional, I did feel slightly deceived. I am very happy with my 2011 Certified Pre-Owned Ford Escape and that's the only reason why I can justify 3 Stars for an experience. However, even the state of my car wasn't ideal after the fact. Considering the regularity of this occurrence, I have a hard time believing that this was not known to the dealership.
